<Date>1565043050087<//Date><Rating>5</Rating>< text>
These guys were really good to me, but I came there knowing exactly what I wanted, and paid cash, so that helped.
The ABS computer was down, they offered to replace it for free.  Had I had to go to Ford and do that myself, I'm fairly certain it would have cost me a pretty penny.  So I'm grateful they took care of that outright from the beginning.  Yes I would recommend this dealer to others.
Their plot of land is small, so they can only fit so much inventory at a time, but vehicles turn over quickly, so check back often.  If they bought the vehicle from auction, just keep your expectations real, and realize that it more likely than not isn't going to be perfect... but with careful research and the Car Fox report... you can make an informed decision.< /text>

<rate>4< /rate>< text>
We played Escape Redding‚Äôs ‚ÄúKnight‚Äù room last night and had a good time. There were 6 of us. 2 newbies and 4 of us who have played Escape games at the other Redding Escape Room locations as well as in other cities. The room was done very well. The setting was awesome and all of the props were very cool. I can definitely appreciate the attention to detail that went into creating the experience. The staff member that helped us along our journey was very pleasant.

During our time in the room... 2 of the required props broke. Both were needed to uncover clues to move forward. The staff member had never encountered the issue and was unsure of what to do. It was a little disappointing for us and negatively impacted our experience and forced us to rush at the end to complete the objective.

I would rate my experience as a 3 Star. However, I am happy and supportive of this new local business and hope to see them thrive which is why I am giving it a 4 star rating. The issues that we encountered were unforeseen and couldn‚Äôt have been reasonably expected but certainly should have been handled differently.</text>

< Review>
Oh, Escape Redding is absolutely FANTASTIC and a total must for anyone who loves escape rooms, and/or riddle games!

While I live in the Bay Area now, I grew up in Redding, and never would have imagined that escape rooms would make it this far up North, nor would I have imagined they would be as well thought out as Escape Redding.

A group of nine of us tried our luck with the "Knight Room" and had an incredible time! IT IS SO COOL. The attention to detail in this room is mind boggling - every clue and every riddle is intricately placed. It was challenging enough but not to the point that you were completely frustrated.

Another major plus is how kind the owners are. You can tell they put their heart into this business and thus charge a totally reasonable $25/person. We'll definitely be coming back to try the other rooms next time we're home!<//Review>

<UserId.>112738251620838872159</UserId.>< name>

<Time>1524368055164</Time><Rating>5</Rating><Review>I will be as honest as possible. I mainly want this review to be seen as a suggestion versus a bad review. We actually had a good time and the staff was friendly. This was the knight.

1. The room where everything is explained before entering the actual room needs to be changed. When I entered this brightly lit room, it took away the suspenseful atmosphere. A bright room just seems like a super happy vibe.
2. In this same room, they used a PowerPoint presentation to explain everything. It kinda felt like being in school, so that too kinda took away the suspenseful vibe. The past host's we've had at different locations were VERY in character and had the script memorized so it felt like we were in an actor's presence. They knew how to set the tone. He was a great guy and all but again, it didn't capture the suspense.
3. There was no background music to help set the tone. No feeling of suspense or the feeling of running out of time. I want my heart racing and i want to be stressing out, lol
4. Another host popped in and out a couple times to help out but it ruined the atmosphere more than anything. When you're at the theater getting lost in the plot, you don't want someone to keep popping in and out, am I right?
5. Some issues with the props. The door was solved by my step dad just by tinkering around with it and not using the clues. That shouldn't be possible. There was a unlocked pad lock that wasn't fastened shut. Host's should double check things like that. There was a missing magnet to complete a task.
6. The tv monitor in the escape room should make like a small beep noise to notify about new information updated on the screen. We get lost in the moment and we don't even think about looking up at the screen.
7. We felt like too many hints had to be given out. The game should make connections quite smoothly. We shouldn't have to depend on the screen. We want to feel that self accomplishment.

We did have fun and I'm open to try another room. I'm not the type to ask for a refund but it would be nice to have a freebie invitation to make up for all the inconveniences that happened that day. Thanks again and I hope this review was helpful.</Review><pics>None< /pics>< Resp>
None</Resp>

< Review>
This is a somewhat small location but it packs a lot of flavor. It's located in a shopping area with a decent amount of dining options. It has the feel of a craft beer joint but the food options really surprised me. I found myself talking about the "Hot Mother Clucker" sandwich for a few days after my visit. It was a spicy battered chicken sandwich with spicy slaw and waffles for the bun. Way fun.</Review>

<rating>1< /rating>< Text>
All my events (ie. Baptisms, comunions, etc.) Have always been at this church. I moved a bit far away and no longer live in town. Four years ago i got married at this church to the man of my dreams. My husband passed last year in the worse way possible. I am still trying to put myself together piece by piece. I recently went there to begin the process of getting my son baptized there, as well as, me just being there was a huge step for me as it brings many memories and i knew would trigger my ptsd. My family still lives in town and he is the only one left to be baptized and i so wanted him to be baptized at the same church i call home. My husbands death has left me with PTSD among other social anxiety problems. When i went there i could not find the office. I knocked on what ever door looked lively and the "father" answered. When i asked for his help he rudely told me..."theres a sign out there" and closed the screen door. I said "excuse im sorry, there are a lot of sign's and im not sure which sign you are talking about." He said "right there in front of the church." (I couldnt even see where he was pointimg to as he didnt even open the screen door.) I said "infornt of the door?" He again in a rude tone said "cant you see it?" I said "no that is why im asking for help." I asked if he was the father and he said "sure am." And i said ok well i think i will go to another church. He said.... "You dont come to church anyways." I was so choked. I said, "i dont live here im from......" He said "who cares you dont come to anyways." I turned and said "if you must know... I witnessed my husband death in the worse way. We were married at this church and its been really difficult for me to be here." He then responded in a condescending manner " oh well...sorry...i didnt know." I dont live there so no i do come to that church anymore but as mentioned i had always had a special place in my heart for that church and was looking forward to celebrating these godly events with my family who still live in town and keeping my whole family under the same church (whatever is left of my family that is) especially since i plan on moving back to town. Instead i left in tears and infuriated. I thought the church is suppose to welcome ANYONE with love? Not just those who regularly attent that particular church. I still tear up at the thought that my son will be the only one not baptized at this church. Thankfully all churches serve the same lord and saver and still can have him baptized under the catholic church which is very much important to me. My parents even got married at this church. Sad to think this new father who i know hasnt been there for five years (as he is not the one who married me and my late husband) turned me away in tears during a time that was very difficult for me and needed my faith more than anything at that very second. Very dissapointed with this new father to say the least. Only regret not video taping him as i was so shoked at his demeaner towards me.< /Text>

< Review>
Stopped by here after our shopping at Westfield ran late, and they were conveniently having reverse happy hour! (Saturday 9pm-close)

THE GOOD
Happy hour prices can‚Äôt be beat. $1 chef choice oysters, a long list of menu items for under $10 (sashimi, carpaccio, sushi rolls, fries, etc). Tbh I probably wouldn‚Äôt come here if not for happy hour just because the regular menu gets pricey and you won‚Äôt feel the freedom to try lots of things.

We liked the salmon and yellowtail carpaccios. Very fresh and flavorful, seasoned well.
Garlic wings were good, no complaints
You can also get sake for cheap happy hour prices

Food came out super fast. Like within 10min all 6 items were on the table.

THE DISAPPOINTING
The oysters were...inconsistent. Some were too briny (borderline unfresh?) others were ok. Hit or miss
Our fries came out lukewarm, and within a couple minutes were starchy and soggy. I hope it was just an off day.< /Review>

<userid>112825600731936006101</userid><Name>Daniel Hynch< /Name><time>1568045407057<//time><Rating>4</Rating>< text>
If you have never been to any of the EMC Seafood Locations I definitely would recommend coming to this one over the LA Ktown location! The location in Ktown always seems to be busy with a wait and parking is definitely a pain there.

This location at the Westfield Santa Anita Mall had no wait time and of course tons of easy parking because it's at a giant mall. Definitely on the smaller side compared to the Ktown location but the restaurant had a pretty chill open air vibe. Felt like I was eating at an open air street market.

We didn't try too many things but here is a breakdown of what we got:

Pros:
-Crispy Pepper Calamari with Spicy Aioli:
This was by far my FAVORITE dish we ordered. Perfect light crispy batter and I really enjoyed the peppers/garlic/and green onion garnish.

-Special: Grilled Tuna Collar:
Great portion for the price. Nice and charred  with a great dipping sauce to accompany it (kind of like a chimichurri).

-Shu Mai:
Not sure if this was a daily thing or just on the weekends (we went on a Sunday). Average size and pretty good flavor. Obviously not going to be as cheap as actual dimsum restaurants.

Cons:
-Har Gow:
Unfortunately I would steer clear of the Har Gow next time. The wrapper on all four of the shrimp dumplings was basically mushy and disintegrated when we went to pick them up.

Overall EMC is a solid dining option when shopping at the Westfield Santa Anita Mall! On the list to try next visit are the fresh oysters and the Uni Pasta!<//text>

< review>
I love Firehouse Subs, and I've been eating them since I was on the east coast.  To me, the serve the perfect sandwich.  The bread is toasted to a nice crisp, the meats are flavorful and juicy, and the flavors are well-balanced, not too salty or sweet.

Among my favorite sandwiches include the Hook and Ladder--the honey ham is simply delicious and adds a savory sweetness to the sandwich that makes it very well balanced, the New York Steamer--probably the best corned beef and pastrami I've had outside of NYC, the Meatball sub, and the brisket sandwich, which has a nice smoky flavor to the brisket slices.  (My friend and I used to often joke it's smokier than most other BBQ joints in San Diego!)  In addition to the sandwiches, the cookies are great.

For any regional or national franchise, Firehouse Subs is definitely my go-to for sandwiches.</review>

TJ's used to be my number one choice, but since the pandemic began, it has become my last choice, and I am pretty much weaned off due to attitude of employees.
